runs a periodic loop to reconcile the desired state of the world with\n    46→// the actual state of the world by triggering attach detach operations.\n    47→// Note: This is distinct from the Reconciler implemented by the kubelet volume\n    48→// manager. This reconciles state for the attach/detach controller. That\n    49→// reconciles state for the kubelet volume manager.\n    50→type Reconciler interface {\n    51→\t// Starts running the reconciliation loop which executes periodically, checks\n    52→\t// if volumes that should be attached are attached and volumes that should\n    53→\t// be detached are detached. If not, it will trigger attach/detach\n    54→\t// operations to rectify.\n    55→\tRun(ctx context.Context)\n    56→}\n    57→\n    58→// NewReconciler returns a new instance of Reconciler that waits loopPeriod\n    59→// between successive executions.\n    60→// loopPeriod is the amount of time the reconciler loop waits between\n    61→// successive executions.\n    62→// maxWaitForUnmountDuration is the max amount of time the reconciler will wait\n    63→// for the volume to be safely unmounted, after this it will detach the volume\n    64→// anyway (to handle crashed/unavailable nodes). If during this time the volume\n    65→// becomes used by a new pod, the detach request will be aborted and the timer\n    66→// cleared.\n    67→func NewReconciler(\n    68→\tloopPeriod time.Duration,\n    69→\tmaxWaitForUnmountDuration time.Duration,\n    70→\tsyncDuration time.Duration,\n    71→\tdisableReconciliationSync bool,\n    72→\tdisableForceDetachOnTimeout bool,\n    73→\tdesiredStateOfWorld cache.DesiredStateOfWorld,\n    74→\tactualStateOfWorld cache.ActualStateOfWorld,\n    75→\tattacherDetacher operationexecutor.OperationExecutor,\n    76→\tnodeStatusUpdater statusupdater.NodeStatusUpdater,\n    77→\tnodeLister corelisters.NodeLister,\n    78→\trecorder record.EventRecorder) Reconciler {\n    79→\treturn &reconciler{\n    80→\t\tloopPeriod:                  loopPeriod,\n    81→\t\tmaxWaitForUnmountDuration:   maxWaitForUnmountDuration,\n    82→\t\tsyncDuration:                syncDuration,\n    83→\t\tdisableReconciliationSync:   disableReconciliationSync,\n    84→\t\tdisableForceDetachOnTimeout: disableForceDetachOnTimeout,\n    85→\t\tdesiredStateOfWorld:         desiredStateOfWorld,\n    86→\t\tactualStateOfWorld:          actualStateOfWorld,\n    87→\t\tattacherDetacher:            attacherDetacher,\n    88→\t\tnodeStatusUpdater:           nodeStatusUpdater,\n    89→\t\tnodeLister:                  nodeLister,\n    90→\t\ttimeOfLastSync:              time.Now(),\n    91→\t\trecorder:                    recorder,\n    92→\t}\n    93→}\n    94→\n    95→type reconciler struct {\n    96→\tloopPeriod                  time.Duration\n    97→\tmaxWaitForUnmountDuration   time.Duration\n    98→\tsyncDuration                time.Duration\n    99→\tdesiredStateOfWorld         cache.DesiredStateOfWorld\n   100→\tactualStateOfWorld          cache.ActualStateOfWorld\n   101→\tattacherDetacher            operationexecutor.OperationExecutor\n   102→\tnodeStatusUpdater           statusupdater.NodeStatusUpdater\n   103→\tnodeLister                  corelisters.NodeLister\n   104→\ttimeOfLastSync              time.Time\n   105→\tdisableReconciliationSync   bool\n   106→\tdisableForceDetachOnTimeout bool\n   107→\trecorder                    record.EventRecorder\n   108→}\n   109→\n   110→func (rc *reconciler) Run(ctx context.Context) {\n   111→\twait.UntilWithContext(ctx, rc.reconciliationLoopFunc(ctx), rc.loopPeriod)\n   112→}\n   113→\n   114→// reconciliationLoopFunc this can be disabled via cli option disableReconciliation.\n   115→// It periodically checks whether the attached volumes from actual state\n   116→// are still attached to the node and update the status if they are not.\n   117→func (rc *reconciler) reconciliationLoopFunc(ctx context.Context) func(context.Context) {\n   118→\treturn func(ctx context.Context) {\n   119→\n   120→\t\trc.reconcile(ctx)\n   121→\t\tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n   122→\t\tif rc.disableReconciliationSync {\n   123→\t\t\tlogger.V(5).Info(\"Skipping reconciling attached volumes still attached since it is disabled via the command line\")\n   124→\t\t} else if rc.syncDuration < time.Second {\n   125→\t\t\tlogger.V(5).Info(\"Skipping reconciling attached volumes still attached since it is set to less than one second via the command line\")\n   126→\t\t} else if time.Since(rc.timeOfLastSync) > rc.syncDuration {\n   127→\t\t\tlogger.V(5).Info(\"Starting reconciling attached volumes still attached\")\n   128→\t\t\trc.sync()\n   129→\t\t}\n   130→\t}\n   131→}\n   132→\n   133→func (rc *reconciler) sync() {\n   134→\tdefer rc.updateSyncTime()\n   135→\trc.syncStates()\n   136→}\n   137→\n   138→func (rc *reconciler) updateSyncTime() {\n   139→\trc.timeOfLastSync = time.Now()\n   140→}\n   141→\n   142→func (rc *reconciler) syncStates() {\n   143→\tvolumesPerNode := rc.actualStateOfWorld.GetAttachedVolumesPerNode()\n   144→\trc.attacherDetacher.VerifyVolumesAreAttached(volumesPerNode, rc.actualStateOfWorld)\n   145→}\n   146→\n   147→// hasOutOfServiceTaint returns true if the node has out-of-service taint present.\n   148→func (rc *reconciler) hasOutOfServiceTaint(nodeName types.NodeName) (bool, error) {\n   149→\tnode, err := rc.nodeLister.Get(string(nodeName))\n   150→\tif err != nil {\n   151→\t\treturn false, err\n   152→\t}\n   153→\treturn taints.TaintKeyExists(node.Spec.Taints, v1.TaintNodeOutOfService), nil\n   154→}\n   155→\n   156→// nodeIsHealthy returns true if the node looks healthy.\n   157→func (rc *reconciler) nodeIsHealthy(nodeName types.NodeName) (bool, error) {\n   158→\tnode, err := rc.nodeLister.Get(string(nodeName))\n   159→\tif err != nil {\n   160→\t\treturn false, err\n   161→\t}\n   162→\treturn nodeutil.IsNodeReady(node), nil\n   163→}\n   164→\n   165→func (rc *reconciler) reconcile(ctx context.Context) {\n   166→\t// Detaches are triggered before attaches so that volumes referenced by\n   167→\t// pods that are rescheduled to a different node are detached first.\n   168→\n   169→\t// Ensure volumes that should be detached are detached.\n   170→\tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n   171→\tfor _, attachedVolume := range rc.actualStateOfWorld.GetAttachedVolumes() {\n   172→\t\tif !rc.desiredStateOfWorld.VolumeExists(\n   173→\t\t\tattachedVolume.VolumeName, attachedVolume.NodeName) {\n   174→\n   175→\t\t\t// Check whether there already exist an operation pending, and don't even\n   176→\t\t\t// try to start an operation if there is already one running.\n   177→\t\t\t// This check must be done before we do any other checks, as otherwise the other checks\n   178→\t\t\t// may pass while at the same time the volume leaves the pending state, resulting in\n   179→\t\t\t// double detach attempts\n   180→\t\t\t// The operation key format is different depending on whether the volume\n   181→\t\t\t// allows multi attach across different nodes.\n   182→\t\t\tif util.IsMultiAttachAllowed(attachedVolume.VolumeSpec) {\n   183→\t\t\t\tif !rc.attacherDetacher.IsOperationSafeToRetry(attachedVolume.VolumeName, \"\" /* podName */, attachedVolume.NodeName, operationexecutor.DetachOperationName) {\n   184→\t\t\t\t\tlogger.V(10).Info(\"Operation for volume is already running or still in exponential backoff for node. Can't start detach\", \"node\", klog.KRef(\"\", string(attachedVolume.NodeName)), \"volumeName\", attachedVolume.VolumeName)\n   185→\t\t\t\t\tcontinue\n   186→\t\t\t\t}\n   187→\t\t\t} else {\n   188→\t\t\t\tif !rc.attacherDetacher.IsOperationSafeToRetry(attachedVolume.VolumeName, \"\" /* podName */, \"\" /* nodeName */, operationexecutor.DetachOperationName) {\n   189→\t\t\t\t\tlogger.V(10).Info(\"Operation for volume is already running or still in exponential backoff in the cluster. Can't start detach for node\", \"node\", klog.KRef(\"\", string(attachedVolume.NodeName)), \"volumeName\", attachedVolume.VolumeName)\n   190→\t\t\t\t\tcontinue\n   191→\t\t\t\t}\n   192→\t\t\t}\n   193→\n   194→\t\t\t// Because the detach operation updates the ActualStateOfWorld before\n   195→\t\t\t// marking itself complete, it's possible for the volume to be removed\n   196→\t\t\t// from the ActualStateOfWorld between the GetAttachedVolumes() check\n   197→\t\t\t// and the IsOperationSafeToRetry() check above.\n   198→\t\t\t// Check the ActualStateOfWorld again to avoid issuing an unnecessary\n   199→\t\t\t// detach.\n   200→\t\t\t// See https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/issues/93902\n   201→\t\t\tattachState := rc.actualStateOfWorld.GetAttachState(attachedVolume.VolumeName, attachedVolume.NodeName)\n   202→\t\t\tif attachState == cache.AttachStateDetached {\n   203→\t\t\t\tlogger.V(5).Info(\"Volume detached--skipping\", \"node\", klog.KRef(\"\", string(attachedVolume.NodeName)), \"volumeName\", attachedVolume.VolumeName)\n   204→\t\t\t\tcontinue\n   205→\t\t\t}\n   206→\n   207→\t\t\t// Set the detach request time\n   208→\t\t\telapsedTime, err := rc.actualStateOfWorld.SetDetachRequestTime(logger, attachedVolume.VolumeName, attachedVolume.NodeName)\n   209→\t\t\tif err != nil {\n   210→\t\t\t\tlogger.Error(err, \"Cannot trigger detach because it fails to set detach request time with error\")\n   211→\t\t\t\tcontinue\n   212→\t\t\t}\n   213→\t\t\t// Check whether the umount drain timer expired\n   214→\t\t\tmaxWaitForUnmountDurationExpired := elapsedTime > rc.maxWaitForUnmountDuration\n   215→\n   216→\t\t\tisHealthy, err := rc.nodeIsHealthy(attachedVolume.NodeName)\n   217→\t\t\tif err != nil {\n   218→\t\t\t\tlogger.Error(err, \"Failed to get health of node\", \"node\", klog.KRef(\"\", string(attachedVolume.NodeName)))\n   219→\t\t\t}\n   220→\n   221→\t\t\t// Force detach volumes from unhealthy nodes after maxWaitForUnmountDuration if force detach is enabled\n   222→\t\t\t// Ensure that the timeout condition checks this correctly so that the correct metric is updated below\n   223→\t\t\tforceDetatchTimeoutExpired := maxWaitForUnmountDurationExpired && !rc.disableForceDetachOnTimeout\n   224→\t\t\tif maxWaitForUnmountDurationExpired && rc.disableForceDetachOnTimeout {\n   225→\t\t\t\tlogger.V(5).Info(\"Drain timeout expired for volume but disableForceDetachOnTimeout was set\", \"node\", klog.KRef(\"\", string(attachedVolume.NodeName)), \"volumeName\", attachedVolume.VolumeName)\n   226→\t\t\t}\n   227→\t\t\tforceDetach := !isHealthy && forceDetatchTimeoutExpired\n   228→\n   229→\t\t\thasOutOfServiceTaint, err := rc.hasOutOfServiceTaint(attachedVolume.NodeName)\n   230→\t\t\tif err != nil {\n   231→\t\t\t\tlogger.Error(err, \"Failed to get taint specs for node\", \"node\", klog.KRef(\"\", string(attachedVolume.NodeName)))\n   232→\t\t\t}\n   233→\n   234→\t\t\t// Check whether volume is still mounted. Skip detach if it is still mounted unless we have\n   235→\t\t\t// decided to force detach or the node has `node.kubernetes.io/out-of-service` taint.\n   236→\t\t\tif attachedVolume.MountedByNode && !forceDetach && !hasOutOfServiceTaint {\n   237→\t\t\t\tlogger.V(5).Info(\"Cannot detach volume because it is still mounted\", \"node\", klog.KRef(\"\", string(attachedVolume.NodeName)), \"volumeName\", attachedVolume.VolumeName)\n   238→\t\t\t\tcontinue\n   239→\t\t\t}\n   240→\n   241→\t\t\t// Before triggering volume detach, mark volume as detached and update the node status\n   242→\t\t\t// If it fails to update node status, skip detach volume\n   243→\t\t\t// If volume detach operation fails, the volume needs to be added back to report as attached so that node status\n   244→\t\t\t// has the correct volume attachment information.\n   245→\t\t\terr = rc.actualStateOfWorld.RemoveVolumeFromReportAsAttached(attachedVolume.VolumeName, attachedVolume.NodeName)\n   246→\t\t\tif err != nil {\n   247→\t\t\t\tlogger.V(5).Info(\"RemoveVolumeFromReportAsAttached failed while removing volume from node\",\n   248→\t\t\t\t\t\"node\", klog.KRef(\"\", string(attachedVolume.NodeName)),\n   249→\t\t\t\t\t\"volumeName\", attachedVolume.VolumeName,\n   250→\t\t\t\t\t\"err\", err)\n   251→\t\t\t}\n   252→\n   253→\t\t\t// Update Node Status to indicate volume is no longer safe to mount.\n   254→\t\t\terr = rc.nodeStatusUpdater.UpdateNodeStatusForNode(logger, attachedVolume.NodeName)\n   255→\t\t\tif err != nil {\n   256→\t\t\t\t// Skip detaching this volume if unable to update node status\n   257→\t\t\t\tlogger.Error(err, \"UpdateNodeStatusForNode failed while attempting to report volume as attached\", \"node\", klog.KRef(\"\", string(attachedVolume.NodeName)), \"volumeName\", attachedVolume.VolumeName)\n   258→\t\t\t\t// Add volume back to ReportAsAttached if UpdateNodeStatusForNode call failed so that node status updater will add it back to VolumeAttached list.\n   259→\t\t\t\t// It is needed here too because DetachVolume is not call actually and we keep the data consistency for every reconcile.\n   260→\t\t\t\trc.actualStateOfWorld.AddVolumeToReportAsAttached(logger, attachedVolume.VolumeName, attachedVolume.NodeName)\n   261→\t\t\t\tcontinue\n   262→\t\t\t}\n   263→\n   264→\t\t\t// Trigger detach volume which requires verifying safe to detach step\n   265→\t\t\t// If forceDetatchTimeoutExpired is true, skip verifySafeToDetach check\n   266→\t\t\t// If the node has node.kubernetes.io/out-of-service taint with NoExecute effect, skip verifySafeToDetach check\n   267→\t\t\tlogger.V(5).Info(\"Starting attacherDetacher.DetachVolume\", \"node\", klog.KRef(\"\", string(attachedVolume.NodeName)), \"volumeName\", attachedVolume.VolumeName)\n   268→\t\t\tif hasOutOfServiceTaint {\n   269→\t\t\t\tlogger.V(4).Info(\"node has out-of-service taint\", \"node\", klog.KRef(\"\", string(attachedVolume.NodeName)))\n   270→\t\t\t}\n   271→\t\t\tverifySafeToDetach := !(forceDetatchTimeoutExpired || hasOutOfServiceTaint)\n   272→\t\t\terr = rc.attacherDetacher.DetachVolume(logger, attachedVolume.AttachedVolume, verifySafeToDetach, rc.actualStateOfWorld)\n   273→\t\t\tif err == nil {\n   274→\t\t\t\tif verifySafeToDetach { // normal detach\n   275→\t\t\t\t\tlogger.Info(\"attacherDetacher.DetachVolume started\", \"node\", klog.KRef(\"\", string(attachedVolume.NodeName)), \"volumeName\", attachedVolume.VolumeName)\n   276→\t\t\t\t} else { // force detach\n   277→\t\t\t\t\tif forceDetatchTimeoutExpired {\n   278→\t\t\t\t\t\tmetrics.RecordForcedDetachMetric(metrics.ForceDetachReasonTimeout)\n   279→\t\t\t\t\t\tlogger.Info(\"attacherDetacher.DetachVolume started: this volume is not safe to detach, but maxWaitForUnmountDuration expired, force detaching\",\n   280→\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\"duration\", rc.maxWaitForUnmountDuration,\n   281→\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\"node\", klog.KRef(\"\", string(attachedVolume.NodeName)),\n   282→\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\"volumeName\", attachedVolume.VolumeName)\n   283→\t\t\t\t\t} else {\n   284→\t\t\t\t\t\tmetrics.RecordForcedDetachMetric(metrics.ForceDetachReasonOutOfService)\n   285→\t\t\t\t\t\tlogger.Info(\"attacherDetacher.DetachVolume started: node has out-of-service taint, force detaching\",\n   286→\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\"node\", klog.KRef(\"\", string(attachedVolume.NodeName)),\n   287→\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\"volumeName\", attachedVolume.VolumeName)\n   288→\t\t\t\t\t}\n   289→\t\t\t\t}\n   290→\t\t\t}\n   291→\t\t\tif err != nil {\n   292→\t\t\t\t// Add volume back to ReportAsAttached if DetachVolume call failed so that node status updater will add it back to VolumeAttached list.\n   293→\t\t\t\t// This function is also called during executing the volume detach operation in operation_generoator.\n   294→\t\t\t\t// It is needed here too because DetachVolume call might fail before executing the actual operation in operation_executor (e.g., cannot find volume plugin etc.)\n   295→\t\t\t\trc.actualStateOfWorld.AddVolumeToReportAsAttached(logger, attachedVolume.VolumeName, attachedVolume.NodeName)\n   296→\n   297→\t\t\t\tif !exponentialbackoff.IsExponentialBackoff(err) {\n   298→\t\t\t\t\t// Ignore exponentialbackoff.IsExponentialBackoff errors, they are expected.\n   299→\t\t\t\t\t// Log all other errors.\n   300→\t\t\t\t\tlogger.Error(err, \"attacherDetacher.DetachVolume failed to start\", \"node\", klog.KRef(\"\", string(attachedVolume.NodeName)), \"volumeName\", attachedVolume.VolumeName)\n   301→\t\t\t\t}\n   302→\t\t\t}\n   303→\t\t}\n   304→\t}\n   305→\n   306→\trc.attachDesiredVolumes(logger)\n   307→\n   308→\t// Update Node Status\n   309→\terr := rc.nodeStatusUpdater.UpdateNodeStatuses(logger)\n   310→\tif err != nil {\n   311→\t\tlogger.Info(\"UpdateNodeStatuses failed\", \"err\", err)\n   312→\t}\n   313→}\n   314→\n   315→func (rc *reconciler) attachDesiredVolumes(logger klog.Logger) {\n   316→\t// Ensure volumes that should be attached are attached.\n   317→\tfor _, volumeToAttach := range rc.desiredStateOfWorld.GetVolumesToAttach() {\n   318→\t\tif util.IsMultiAttachAllowed(volumeToAttach.VolumeSpec) {\n   319→\t\t\t// Don't even try to start an operation if there is already one running for the given volume and node.\n   320→\t\t\tif rc.attacherDetacher.IsOperationPending(volumeToAttach.VolumeName, \"\" /* podName */, volumeToAttach.NodeName) {\n   321→\t\t\t\tlogger.V(10).Info(\"Operation for volume is already running for node. Can't start attach\", \"node\", klog.KRef(\"\", string(volumeToAttach.NodeName)), \"volumeName\", volumeToAttach.VolumeName)\n   322→\t\t\t\tcontinue\n   323→\t\t\t}\n   324→\t\t} else {\n   325→\t\t\t// Don't even try to start an operation if there is already one running for the given volume\n   326→\t\t\tif rc.attacherDetacher.IsOperationPending(volumeToAttach.VolumeName, \"\" /* podName */, \"\" /* nodeName */) {\n   327→\t\t\t\tlogger.V(10).Info(\"Operation for volume is already running. Can't start attach for node\", \"node\", klog.KRef(\"\", string(volumeToAttach.NodeName)), \"volumeNames\", volumeToAttach.VolumeName)\n   328→\t\t\t\tcontinue\n   329→\t\t\t}\n   330→\t\t}\n   331→\n   332→\t\t// Because the attach operation updates the ActualStateOfWorld before\n   333→\t\t// marking itself complete, IsOperationPending() must be checked before\n   334→\t\t// GetAttachState() to guarantee the ActualStateOfWorld is\n   335→\t\t// up-to-date when it's read.\n   336→\t\t// See https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/issues/93902\n   337→\t\tattachState := rc.actualStateOfWorld.GetAttachState(volumeToAttach.VolumeName, volumeToAttach.NodeName)\n   338→\t\tif attachState == cache.AttachStateAttached {\n   339→\t\t\t// Volume/Node exists, touch it to 349→\t\t\t\t\trc.reportMultiAttachError(logger, volumeToAttach, nodes)\n   350→\t\t\t\t\trc.desiredStateOfWorld.SetMultiAttachError(volumeToAttach.VolumeName, volumeToAttach.NodeName)\n   351→\t\t\t\t}\n   352→\t\t\t\tcontinue\n   353→\t\t\t}\n   354→\t\t}\n   355→\n   356→\t\t// Volume/Node doesn't exist, spawn a goroutine to attach it\n   357→\t\tlogger.V(5).Info(\"Starting {\n   360→\t\t\tlogger.Info(\"attacherDetacher.AttachVolume started\", \"volumeName\", volumeToAttach.VolumeName, \"nodeName\", volumeToAttach.NodeName, \"scheduledPods\", klog.KObjSlice(volumeToAttach.ScheduledPods))\n   361→\t\t}\n   362→\t\tif err != nil && !exponentialbackoff.IsExponentialBackoff(err) {\n   363→\t\t\t// Ignore exponentialbackoff.IsExponentialBackoff errors, they are expected.\n   364→\t\t\t// Log all other errors.\n   365→\t\t\tlogger.Error(err, \"attacherDetacher.AttachVolume failed to start\", \"volumeName\", volumeToAttach.VolumeName, \"nodeName\", volumeToAttach.NodeName, \"scheduledPods\", klog.KObjSlice(volumeToAttach.ScheduledPods))\n   366→\t\t}\n   367→\t}\n   368→}\n   369→\n   370→// reportMultiAttachError sends events and logs situation that a volume that\n   371→// should be attached to a node is already attached to different node(s).\n   372→func (rc *reconciler) reportMultiAttachError(logger klog.Logger, volumeToAttach cache.VolumeToAttach, nodes []types.NodeName) {\n   373→\t// Filter out the current node from list of nodes where the volume is\n   374→\t// attached.\n   375→\t// Some methods need []string, some other needs []NodeName, collect both.\n   376→\t// In theory, these arrays should have always only one element - the\n   377→\t// controller does not allow more than one attachment. But use array just\n   378→\t// in case...\n   379→\totherNodes := []types.NodeName{}\n   380→\totherNodesStr := []string{}\n   381→\tfor _, node := range nodes {\n   382→\t\tif node != volumeToAttach.NodeName {\n   383→\t\t\totherNodes = append(otherNodes, node)\n   384→\t\t\totherNodesStr = append(otherNodesStr, string(node))\n   385→\t\t}\n   386→\t}\n   387→\n   388→\t// Get list of pods that use the volume on the other nodes.\n   389→\tpods := rc.desiredStateOfWorld.GetVolumePodsOnNodes(otherNodes, volumeToAttach.VolumeName)\n   390→\tif len(pods) == 0 {\n   391→\t\t// We did not find any pods that requests the volume. The pod must have been deleted already.\n   392→\t\tsimpleMsg, _ := volumeToAttach.GenerateMsg(\"Multi-Attach error\", \"Volume is already exclusively attached to one node and can't be attached to another\")\n   393→\t\tfor _, pod := range volumeToAttach.ScheduledPods {\n   394→\t\t\trc.recorder.Eventf(pod, v1.EventTypeWarning, kevents.FailedAttachVolume, simpleMsg)\n   395→\t\t}\n   396→\t\t// Log detailed message to system admin\n   397→\t\tlogger.Info(\"Multi-Attach error: volume is already exclusively attached and can't be attached to another node\", \"attachedTo\", otherNodesStr, \"volume\", volumeToAttach)\n   398→\t\treturn\n   399→\t}\n   400→\n   401→\t// There are pods that require the volume and run on another node. Typically\n   402→\t// it's user error, e.g. a ReplicaSet uses a PVC and has >1 replicas. Let\n   403→\t// the user know what pods are blocking the volume.\n   404→\tfor _, scheduledPod := range volumeToAttach.ScheduledPods {\n   405→\t\t// Each scheduledPod must get a custom message. They can run in\n   406→\t\t// different namespaces and user of a namespace should not see names of\n   407→\t\t// pods in other namespaces.\n   408→\t\tlocalPodNames := []string{} // Names of pods in scheduledPods's namespace\n   409→\t\totherPods := 0              // Count of pods in other namespaces\n   410→\t\tfor _, pod := range pods {\n   411→\t\t\tif pod.Namespace == scheduledPod.Namespace {\n   412→\t\t\t\tlocalPodNames = append(localPodNames, pod.Name)\n   413→\t\t\t} else {\n   414→\t\t\t\totherPods++\n   415→\t\t\t}\n   416→\t\t}\n   417→\n   418→\t\tvar msg string\n   419→\t\tif len(localPodNames) > 0 {\n   420→\t\t\tmsg = fmt.Sprintf(\"Volume is already used by pod(s) %s\", strings.Join(localPodNames, \", \"))\n   421→\t\t\tif otherPods > 0 {\n   422→\t\t\t\tmsg = fmt.Sprintf(\"%s and %d pod(s) in different namespaces\", msg, otherPods)\n   423→\t\t\t}\n   424→\t\t} else {\n   425→\t\t\t// No local pods, there are pods only in different namespaces.\n   426→\t\t\tmsg = fmt.Sprintf(\"Volume is already used by %d pod(s) in different namespaces\", otherPods)\n   427→\t\t}\n   428→\t\tsimpleMsg, _ := volumeToAttach.GenerateMsg(\"Multi-Attach error\", msg)\n   429→\t\trc.recorder.Eventf(scheduledPod, v1.EventTypeWarning, kevents.FailedAttachVolume, simpleMsg)\n   430→\t}\n   431→\n   432→\t// Log all pods for system admin\n   433→\tlogger.Info(\"Multi-Attach error: volume is already used by pods\", \"pods\", klog.KObjSlice(pods), \"attachedTo\", otherNodesStr, \"volume\", volumeToAttach)\n   434→}\n   435→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. (\n\t\"context\"\n\t\"fmt\"\n\t\"strings\"\n\t\"time\"\n\n\tv1 \"k8s.io/api/core/v1\"\n\t\"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/types\"\n\t\"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/wait\"\n\tcorelisters runs a periodic loop to reconcile the desired state of the world with\n// the actual state of the world by triggering attach detach operations.\n// Note: This is distinct from the Reconciler implemented by the kubelet volume\n// manager. This reconciles state for the attach/detach controller. That\n// reconciles state for the kubelet volume manager.\ntype Reconciler interface {\n\t// Starts running the reconciliation loop which executes periodically, checks\n\t// if volumes that should be attached are attached and volumes that should\n\t// be detached are detached. If not, it will trigger attach/detach\n\t// operations to rectify.\n\tRun(ctx context.Context)\n}\n\n// NewReconciler returns a new instance of Reconciler that waits loopPeriod\n// between successive executions.\n// loopPeriod is the amount of time the reconciler loop waits between\n// successive executions.\n// maxWaitForUnmountDuration is the max amount of time the reconciler will wait\n// for the volume to be safely unmounted, after this it will detach the volume\n// anyway (to handle crashed/unavailable nodes). If during this time the volume\n// becomes used by a new pod, the detach request will be aborted and the timer\n// cleared.\nfunc NewReconciler(\n\tloopPeriod time.Duration,\n\tmaxWaitForUnmountDuration time.Duration,\n\tsyncDuration time.Duration,\n\tdisableReconciliationSync bool,\n\tdisableForceDetachOnTimeout bool,\n\tdesiredStateOfWorld cache.DesiredStateOfWorld,\n\tactualStateOfWorld cache.ActualStateOfWorld,\n\tattacherDetacher operationexecutor.OperationExecutor,\n\tnodeStatusUpdater statusupdater.NodeStatusUpdater,\n\tnodeLister corelisters.NodeLister,\n\trecorder record.EventRecorder) Reconciler {\n\treturn &reconciler{\n\t\tloopPeriod:                  loopPeriod,\n\t\tmaxWaitForUnmountDuration:   maxWaitForUnmountDuration,\n\t\tsyncDuration:                syncDuration,\n\t\tdisableReconciliationSync:   disableReconciliationSync,\n\t\tdisableForceDetachOnTimeout: disableForceDetachOnTimeout,\n\t\tdesiredStateOfWorld:         desiredStateOfWorld,\n\t\tactualStateOfWorld:          actualStateOfWorld,\n\t\tattacherDetacher:            attacherDetacher,\n\t\tnodeStatusUpdater:           nodeStatusUpdater,\n\t\tnodeLister:                  nodeLister,\n\t\ttimeOfLastSync:              time.Now(),\n\t\trecorder:                    recorder,\n\t}\n}\n\ntype reconciler struct {\n\tloopPeriod                  time.Duration\n\tmaxWaitForUnmountDuration   time.Duration\n\tsyncDuration                time.Duration\n\tdesiredStateOfWorld         cache.DesiredStateOfWorld\n\tactualStateOfWorld          cache.ActualStateOfWorld\n\tattacherDetacher            operationexecutor.OperationExecutor\n\tnodeStatusUpdater           statusupdater.NodeStatusUpdater\n\tnodeLister                  corelisters.NodeLister\n\ttimeOfLastSync              time.Time\n\tdisableReconciliationSync   bool\n\tdisableForceDetachOnTimeout bool\n\trecorder                    record.EventRecorder\n}\n\nfunc (rc *reconciler) Run(ctx context.Context) {\n\twait.UntilWithContext(ctx, rc.reconciliationLoopFunc(ctx), rc.loopPeriod)\n}\n\n// reconciliationLoopFunc this can be disabled via cli option disableReconciliation.\n// It periodically checks whether the attached volumes from actual state\n// are still attached to the node and update the status if they are not.\nfunc (rc *reconciler) reconciliationLoopFunc(ctx context.Context) func(context.Context) {\n\treturn func(ctx context.Context) {\n\n\t\trc.reconcile(ctx)\n\t\tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n\t\tif rc.disableReconciliationSync {\n\t\t\tlogger.V(5).Info(\"Skipping reconciling attached volumes still attached since it is disabled via the command line\")\n\t\t} else if rc.syncDuration < time.Second {\n\t\t\tlogger.V(5).Info(\"Skipping reconciling attached volumes still attached since it is set to less than one second via the command line\")\n\t\t} else if time.Since(rc.timeOfLastSync) > rc.syncDuration {\n\t\t\tlogger.V(5).Info(\"Starting reconciling attached volumes still attached\")\n\t\t\trc.sync()\n\t\t}\n\t}\n}\n\nfunc (rc *reconciler) sync() {\n\tdefer rc.updateSyncTime()\n\trc.syncStates()\n}\n\nfunc (rc *reconciler) updateSyncTime() {\n\trc.timeOfLastSync = time.Now()\n}\n\nfunc (rc *reconciler) syncStates() {\n\tvolumesPerNode := rc.actualStateOfWorld.GetAttachedVolumesPerNode()\n\trc.attacherDetacher.VerifyVolumesAreAttached(volumesPerNode, rc.actualStateOfWorld)\n}\n\n// hasOutOfServiceTaint returns true if the node has out-of-service taint present.\nfunc (rc *reconciler) hasOutOfServiceTaint(nodeName types.NodeName) (bool, error) {\n\tnode, err := rc.nodeLister.Get(string(nodeName))\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn false, err\n\t}\n\treturn taints.TaintKeyExists(node.Spec.Taints, v1.TaintNodeOutOfService), nil\n}\n\n// nodeIsHealthy returns true if the node looks healthy.\nfunc (rc *reconciler) nodeIsHealthy(nodeName types.NodeName) (bool, error) {\n\tnode, err := rc.nodeLister.Get(string(nodeName))\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn false, err\n\t}\n\treturn nodeutil.IsNodeReady(node), nil\n}\n\nfunc (rc *reconciler) reconcile(ctx context.Context) {\n\t// Detaches are triggered before attaches so that volumes referenced by\n\t// pods that are rescheduled to a different node are detached first.\n\n\t// Ensure volumes that should be detached are detached.\n\tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n\tfor _, attachedVolume := range rc.actualStateOfWorld.GetAttachedVolumes() {\n\t\tif !rc.desiredStateOfWorld.VolumeExists(\n\t\t\tattachedVolume.VolumeName, attachedVolume.NodeName) {\n\n\t\t\t// Check whether there already exist an operation pending, and don't even\n\t\t\t// try to start an operation if there is already one running.\n\t\t\t// This check must be done before we do any other checks, as otherwise the other checks\n\t\t\t// may pass while at the same time the volume leaves the pending state, resulting in\n\t\t\t// double detach attempts\n\t\t\t// The operation key format is different depending on whether the volume\n\t\t\t// allows multi attach across different nodes.\n\t\t\tif util.IsMultiAttachAllowed(attachedVolume.VolumeSpec) {\n\t\t\t\tif !rc.attacherDetacher.IsOperationSafeToRetry(attachedVolume.VolumeName, \"\" /* podName */, attachedVolume.NodeName, operationexecutor.DetachOperationName) {\n\t\t\t\t\tlogger.V(10).Info(\"Operation for volume is already running or still in exponential backoff for node. Can't start detach\", \"node\", klog.KRef(\"\", string(attachedVolume.NodeName)), \"volumeName\", attachedVolume.VolumeName)\n\t\t\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t} else {\n\t\t\t\tif !rc.attacherDetacher.IsOperationSafeToRetry(attachedVolume.VolumeName, \"\" /* podName */, \"\" /* nodeName */, operationexecutor.DetachOperationName) {\n\t\t\t\t\tlogger.V(10).Info(\"Operation for volume is already running or still in exponential backoff in the cluster. Can't start detach for node\", \"node\", klog.KRef(\"\", string(attachedVolume.NodeName)), \"volumeName\", attachedVolume.VolumeName)\n\t\t\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t}\n\n\t\t\t// Because the detach operation updates the ActualStateOfWorld before\n\t\t\t// marking itself complete, it's possible for the volume to be removed\n\t\t\t// from the ActualStateOfWorld between the GetAttachedVolumes() check\n\t\t\t// and the IsOperationSafeToRetry() check above.\n\t\t\t// Check the ActualStateOfWorld again to avoid issuing an unnecessary\n\t\t\t// detach.\n\t\t\t// See https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/issues/93902\n\t\t\tattachState := rc.actualStateOfWorld.GetAttachState(attachedVolume.VolumeName, attachedVolume.NodeName)\n\t\t\tif attachState == cache.AttachStateDetached {\n\t\t\t\tlogger.V(5).Info(\"Volume detached--skipping\", \"node\", klog.KRef(\"\", string(attachedVolume.NodeName)), \"volumeName\", attachedVolume.VolumeName)\n\t\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t\t}\n\n\t\t\t// Set the detach request time\n\t\t\telapsedTime, err := rc.actualStateOfWorld.SetDetachRequestTime(logger, attachedVolume.VolumeName, attachedVolume.NodeName)\n\t\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\t\tlogger.Error(err, \"Cannot trigger detach because it fails to set detach request time with error\")\n\t\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t// Check whether the umount drain timer expired\n\t\t\tmaxWaitForUnmountDurationExpired := elapsedTime > rc.maxWaitForUnmountDuration\n\n\t\t\tisHealthy, err := rc.nodeIsHealthy(attachedVolume.NodeName)\n\t\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\t\tlogger.Error(err, \"Failed to get health of node\", \"node\", klog.KRef(\"\", string(attachedVolume.NodeName)))\n\t\t\t}\n\n\t\t\t// Force detach volumes from unhealthy nodes after maxWaitForUnmountDuration if force detach is enabled\n\t\t\t// Ensure that the timeout condition checks this correctly so that the correct metric is updated below\n\t\t\tforceDetatchTimeoutExpired := maxWaitForUnmountDurationExpired && !rc.disableForceDetachOnTimeout\n\t\t\tif maxWaitForUnmountDurationExpired && rc.disableForceDetachOnTimeout {\n\t\t\t\tlogger.V(5).Info(\"Drain timeout expired for volume but disableForceDetachOnTimeout was set\", \"node\", klog.KRef(\"\", string(attachedVolume.NodeName)), \"volumeName\", attachedVolume.VolumeName)\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tforceDetach := !isHealthy && forceDetatchTimeoutExpired\n\n\t\t\thasOutOfServiceTaint, err := rc.hasOutOfServiceTaint(attachedVolume.NodeName)\n\t\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\t\tlogger.Error(err, \"Failed to get taint specs for node\", \"node\", klog.KRef(\"\", string(attachedVolume.NodeName)))\n\t\t\t}\n\n\t\t\t// Check whether volume is still mounted. Skip detach if it is still mounted unless we have\n\t\t\t// decided to force detach or the node has `node.kubernetes.io/out-of-service` taint.\n\t\t\tif attachedVolume.MountedByNode && !forceDetach && !hasOutOfServiceTaint {\n\t\t\t\tlogger.V(5).Info(\"Cannot detach volume because it is still mounted\", \"node\", klog.KRef(\"\", string(attachedVolume.NodeName)), \"volumeName\", attachedVolume.VolumeName)\n\t\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t\t}\n\n\t\t\t// Before triggering volume detach, mark volume as detached and update the node status\n\t\t\t// If it fails to update node status, skip detach volume\n\t\t\t// If volume detach operation fails, the volume needs to be added back to report as attached so that node status\n\t\t\t// has the correct volume attachment information.\n\t\t\terr = rc.actualStateOfWorld.RemoveVolumeFromReportAsAttached(attachedVolume.VolumeName, attachedVolume.NodeName)\n\t\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\t\tlogger.V(5).Info(\"RemoveVolumeFromReportAsAttached failed while removing volume from node\",\n\t\t\t\t\t\"node\", klog.KRef(\"\", string(attachedVolume.NodeName)),\n\t\t\t\t\t\"volumeName\", attachedVolume.VolumeName,\n\t\t\t\t\t\"err\", err)\n\t\t\t}\n\n\t\t\t// Update Node Status to indicate volume is no longer safe to mount.\n\t\t\terr = rc.nodeStatusUpdater.UpdateNodeStatusForNode(logger, attachedVolume.NodeName)\n\t\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\t\t// Skip detaching this volume if unable to update node status\n\t\t\t\tlogger.Error(err, \"UpdateNodeStatusForNode failed while attempting to report volume as attached\", \"node\", klog.KRef(\"\", string(attachedVolume.NodeName)), \"volumeName\", attachedVolume.VolumeName)\n\t\t\t\t// Add volume back to ReportAsAttached if UpdateNodeStatusForNode call failed so that node status updater will add it back to VolumeAttached list.\n\t\t\t\t// It is needed here too because DetachVolume is not call actually and we keep the data consistency for every reconcile.\n\t\t\t\trc.actualStateOfWorld.AddVolumeToReportAsAttached(logger, attachedVolume.VolumeName, attachedVolume.NodeName)\n\t\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t\t}\n\n\t\t\t// Trigger detach volume which requires verifying safe to detach step\n\t\t\t// If forceDetatchTimeoutExpired is true, skip verifySafeToDetach check\n\t\t\t// If the node has node.kubernetes.io/out-of-service taint with NoExecute effect, skip verifySafeToDetach check\n\t\t\tlogger.V(5).Info(\"Starting attacherDetacher.DetachVolume\", \"node\", klog.KRef(\"\", string(attachedVolume.NodeName)), \"volumeName\", attachedVolume.VolumeName)\n\t\t\tif hasOutOfServiceTaint {\n\t\t\t\tlogger.V(4).Info(\"node has out-of-service taint\", \"node\", klog.KRef(\"\", string(attachedVolume.NodeName)))\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tverifySafeToDetach := !(forceDetatchTimeoutExpired || hasOutOfServiceTaint)\n\t\t\terr = rc.attacherDetacher.DetachVolume(logger, attachedVolume.AttachedVolume, verifySafeToDetach, rc.actualStateOfWorld)\n\t\t\tif err == nil {\n\t\t\t\tif verifySafeToDetach { // normal detach\n\t\t\t\t\tlogger.Info(\"attacherDetacher.DetachVolume started\", \"node\", klog.KRef(\"\", string(attachedVolume.NodeName)), \"volumeName\", attachedVolume.VolumeName)\n\t\t\t\t} else { // force detach\n\t\t\t\t\tif forceDetatchTimeoutExpired {\n\t\t\t\t\t\tmetrics.RecordForcedDetachMetric(metrics.ForceDetachReasonTimeout)\n\t\t\t\t\t\tlogger.Info(\"attacherDetacher.DetachVolume started: this volume is not safe to detach, but maxWaitForUnmountDuration expired, force detaching\",\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\"duration\", rc.maxWaitForUnmountDuration,\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\"node\", klog.KRef(\"\", string(attachedVolume.NodeName)),\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\"volumeName\", attachedVolume.VolumeName)\n\t\t\t\t\t} else {\n\t\t\t\t\t\tmetrics.RecordForcedDetachMetric(metrics.ForceDetachReasonOutOfService)\n\t\t\t\t\t\tlogger.Info(\"attacherDetacher.DetachVolume started: node has out-of-service taint, force detaching\",\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\"node\", klog.KRef(\"\", string(attachedVolume.NodeName)),\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\"volumeName\", attachedVolume.VolumeName)\n\t\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\t\t// Add volume back to ReportAsAttached if DetachVolume call failed so that node status updater will add it back to VolumeAttached list.\n\t\t\t\t// This function is also called during executing the volume detach operation in operation_generoator.\n\t\t\t\t// It is needed here too because DetachVolume call might fail before executing the actual operation in operation_executor (e.g., cannot find volume plugin etc.)\n\t\t\t\trc.actualStateOfWorld.AddVolumeToReportAsAttached(logger, attachedVolume.VolumeName, attachedVolume.NodeName)\n\n\t\t\t\tif !exponentialbackoff.IsExponentialBackoff(err) {\n\t\t\t\t\t// Ignore exponentialbackoff.IsExponentialBackoff errors, they are expected.\n\t\t\t\t\t// Log all other errors.\n\t\t\t\t\tlogger.Error(err, \"attacherDetacher.DetachVolume failed to start\", \"node\", klog.KRef(\"\", string(attachedVolume.NodeName)), \"volumeName\", attachedVolume.VolumeName)\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\trc.attachDesiredVolumes(logger)\n\n\t// Update Node Status\n\terr := rc.nodeStatusUpdater.UpdateNodeStatuses(logger)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\tlogger.Info(\"UpdateNodeStatuses failed\", \"err\", err)\n\t}\n}\n\nfunc (rc *reconciler) attachDesiredVolumes(logger klog.Logger) {\n\t// Ensure volumes that should be attached are if there is already one running for the given volume and node.\n\t\t\tif rc.attacherDetacher.IsOperationPending(volumeToAttach.VolumeName, \"\" /* podName */, volumeToAttach.NodeName) expected.\n\t\t\t// Log all other errors.\n\t\t\tlogger.Error(err, \"attacherDetacher.AttachVolume failed to start\", \"volumeName\", volumeToAttach.VolumeName, \"nodeName\", volumeToAttach.NodeName, \"scheduledPods\", klog.KObjSlice(volumeToAttach.ScheduledPods))\n\t\t}\n\t}\n}\n\n// reportMultiAttachError sends events and logs situation that a volume that\n// should be attached to a node is already attached to different node(s).\nfunc (rc *reconciler) reportMultiAttachError(logger klog.Logger, volumeToAttach cache.VolumeToAttach, nodes []types.NodeName) {\n\t// Filter out the current node from list of nodes where the volume is\n\t// attached.\n\t// Some methods need []string, some other needs []NodeName, collect both.\n\t// In theory, these arrays should have always only one element - the\n\t// controller does not allow more than one attachment. But use array just\n\t// in case...\n\totherNodes := []types.NodeName{}\n\totherNodesStr := []string{}\n\tfor _, node := range nodes {\n\t\tif node != volumeToAttach.NodeName {\n\t\t\totherNodes = append(otherNodes, node)\n\t\t\totherNodesStr = append(otherNodesStr, string(node))\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\t// Get list of pods that use the volume on the other nodes.\n\tpods := rc.desiredStateOfWorld.GetVolumePodsOnNodes(otherNodes, volumeToAttach.VolumeName)\n\tif len(pods) == 0 {\n\t\t// We did not find any pods that requests the volume. The pod must have been deleted already.\n\t\tsimpleMsg, _ := volumeToAttach.GenerateMsg(\"Multi-Attach error\", \"Volume is already exclusively attached to one node and can't be attached to another\")\n\t\tfor _, pod := range volumeToAttach.ScheduledPods {\n\t\t\trc.recorder.Eventf(pod, v1.EventTypeWarning, kevents.FailedAttachVolume, simpleMsg)\n\t\t}\n\t\t// Log detailed message to system admin\n\t\tlogger.Info(\"Multi-Attach error: volume is already exclusively attached and can't be attached to another node\", \"attachedTo\", otherNodesStr, \"volume\", volumeToAttach)\n\t\treturn\n\t}\n\n\t// There are pods that require the volume and run on another node. Typically\n\t// it's user error, e.g. a ReplicaSet uses a PVC and has >1 replicas. Let\n\t// the user know what pods are blocking the volume.\n\tfor _, scheduledPod := range volumeToAttach.ScheduledPods {\n\t\t// Each scheduledPod must get a custom message. They can run in\n\t\t// different namespaces and user of a namespace should not see names of\n\t\t// pods in other namespaces.\n\t\tlocalPodNames := []string{} // Names of pods in scheduledPods's namespace\n\t\totherPods := 0              // Count of pods in other namespaces\n\t\tfor _, pod := range pods {\n\t\t\tif pod.Namespace == scheduledPod.Namespace {\n\t\t\t\tlocalPodNames = append(localPodNames, pod.Name)\n\t\t\t} else {\n\t\t\t\totherPods++\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tvar msg string\n\t\tif len(localPodNames) > 0 {\n\t\t\tmsg = fmt.Sprintf(\"Volume is already used by pod(s) %s\", strings.Join(localPodNames, \", \"))\n\t\t\tif otherPods > 0 {\n\t\t\t\tmsg = fmt.Sprintf(\"%s and %d pod(s) in different namespaces\", msg, otherPods)\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t} else {\n\t\t\t// No local pods, there are pods only in different namespaces.\n\t\t\tmsg = fmt.Sprintf(\"Volume is already used by %d pod(s) in different namespaces\", otherPods)\n\t\t}\n\t\tsimpleMsg, _ := volumeToAttach.GenerateMsg(\"Multi-Attach error\", msg)\n\t\trc.recorder.Eventf(scheduledPod, v1.EventTypeWarning, kevents.FailedAttachVolume, simpleMsg)\n\t}\n\n\t// Log all pods for system admin\n\tlogger.Info(\"Multi-Attach error: volume is already used by pods\", \"pods\", klog.KObjSlice(pods), \"attachedTo\", otherNodesStr, \"volume\", volumeToAttach)\n}\n","numLines":435,"startLine":1,"totalLines":435}}}

The controllers are registered via ControllerDescriptor which contains an initFunc. The pattern in kubernetes is:\n\n1. ControllerDescriptor contains the controller name and initFunc\n2. ReconcileEndpoints; therefore, to understand this, you need only\n    53→// understand the requirements and the body of this function.\n    54→//\n    55→// Requirements:\n    56→//   - All apiservers MUST use the same ports for their {rw, ro} services.\n    57→//   - All apiservers MUST use ReconcileEndpoints and only ReconcileEndpoints to manage the\n    58→//     endpoints for their {rw, ro} from all apiservers.\n    62→func (r *masterCountEndpointReconciler) ReconcileEndpoints(serviceName string, ip net.IP, endpointPorts []corev1.EndpointPort, reconcilePorts bool) error {\n    63→\tr.reconcilingLock.Lock()\n    64→\tdefer r.reconcilingLock.Unlock()\n    65→\n    66→\tif r.stopReconcilingCalled {\n    67→\t\treturn nil\n    68→\t}\n    69→\n    70→\te, err := Given the requirements stated at the top of\n   120→\t\t// this function, this should cause the list of IP addresses to\n   121→\t\t// become eventually correct.\n   122→\t\tif addrs := ip.String() {\n   126→\t\t\t\t\tfor len(*addrs) > r.masterCount {\n   127→\t\t\t\t\t\t// wrap around if necessary.\n   128→\t\t\t\t\t\tremove := (i + 1) % len(*addrs)\n   129→\t\t\t\t\t\t*addrs = append((*addrs)[:remove], (*addrs)[remove+1:]...)\n   130→\t\t\t\t\t}\n   131→\t\t\t\t\tbreak\n   132→\t\t\t\t}\n   133→\t\t\t}\n   134→\t\t}\n   135→\t}\n   136→\tif !portsCorrect {\n   137→\t\t// 57→\t// eventRecorder allows Reconciler to record and publish events.\n    58→\teventRecorder  record.EventRecorder\n    59→\tcontrollerName string\n    60→}\n    61→\n    62→type ReconcilerOption func(*Reconciler)\n    63→\n    64→// WithTrafficDistributionEnabled controls whether the Reconciler considers the\n    65→// `trafficDistribution` field while reconciling EndpointSlices.\n    66→func WithTrafficDistributionEnabled(enabled bool) ReconcilerOption {\n    67→\treturn func(r *Reconciler) {\n    68→\t\tr.trafficDistributionEnabled = enabled\n    69→\t}\n    70→}\n    71→\n    72→// endpointMeta includes the attributes we group slices on, this type helps with\n    73→// that logic in Reconciler\n    74→type endpointMeta struct {\n    75→\tports       []discovery.EndpointPort\n    76→\taddressType discovery.AddressType\n    77→}\n    78→\n    79→// Reconcile takes a set of pods currently matching a service selector and\n    80→// compares them with the endpoints already present in any existing endpoint\n    81→// slices for the given service. It creates, updates, or deletes endpoint slices\n    82→// to ensure the desired set of pods are represented by endpoint slices.\n    83→func (r *Reconciler) Reconcile(logger klog.Logger, service *corev1.Service, pods []*corev1.Pod, existingSlices []*discovery.EndpointSlice, triggerTime time.Time) error {\n    84→\tslicesToDelete := []*discovery.EndpointSlice{}                                    // slices that are no longer  matching any address the service has\n    85→\terrs := []error{}                                                                 // all errors generated in the process of reconciling\n    86→\tslicesByAddressType := make(map[discovery.AddressType][]*discovery.EndpointSlice) // slices by address type\n    87→\n    88→\t// addresses that this service supports [o(1) find]\n    89→\tserviceSupportedAddressesTypes := getAddressTypesForService(logger, service)\n    90→\n    91→\t// loop through slices identifying their address type.\n    92→\t// slices that no longer match address type supported by services\n    93→\t// go to delete, other slices goes to the Reconciler machinery\n    94→\t// for further adjustment\n    95→\tfor _, existingSlice := range existingSlices {\n    96→\t\t// service no longer supports that address type, add it to deleted slices\n    97→\t\tif !serviceSupportedAddressesTypes.Has(existingSlice.AddressType) {\n    98→\t\t\tif r.topologyCache != nil {\n    99→\t\t\t\tsvcKey, err := ServiceControllerKey(existingSlice)\n   100→\t\t\t\tif err != nil {\n   101→\t\t\t\t\tlogger.Info(\"Couldn't get key to remove EndpointSlice from topology cache\", \"existingSlice\", existingSlice, \"err\", err)\n   102→\t\t\t\t} else {\n   103→\t\t\t\t\tr.topologyCache.RemoveHints(svcKey, existingSlice.AddressType)\n   104→\t\t\t\t}\n   105→\t\t\t}\n   106→\n   107→\t\t\tslicesToDelete = append(slicesToDelete, existingSlice)\n   108→\t\t\tcontinue\n   109→\t\t}\n   110→\n   111→\t\t// add list if it is not on our map\n   112→\t\tif _, ok := slicesByAddressType[existingSlice.AddressType]; !ok {\n   113→\t\t\tslicesByAddressType[existingSlice.AddressType] = make([]*discovery.EndpointSlice, 0, 1)\n   114→\t\t}\n   115→\n   116→\t\tslicesByAddressType[existingSlice.AddressType] = append(slicesByAddressType[existingSlice.AddressType], existingSlice)\n   117→\t}\n   118→\n   119→\t// reconcile for existing.\n   120→\tfor addressType := range serviceSupportedAddressesTypes {\n   121→\t\texistingSlices := slicesByAddressType[addressType]\n   122→\t\terr := r.reconcileByAddressType(logger, service, pods, existingSlices, triggerTime, addressType)\n   123→\t\tif err != nil {\n   124→\t\t\terrs = append(errs, err)\n   125→\t\t}\n   126→\t}\n   127→\n   128→\t// delete those which are of addressType that is no longer supported\n   129→\t// by the service\n   130→\tfor _, sliceToDelete := range slicesToDelete {\n   131→\t\terr := r.client.DiscoveryV1().EndpointSlices(service.Namespace).Delete(context.TODO(), sliceToDelete.Name, metav1.DeleteOptions{})\n   132→\t\tif err != nil {\n   133→\t\t\terrs = append(errs, fmt.Errorf(\"error deleting %s EndpointSlice for Service %s/%s: %w\", sliceToDelete.Name, service.Namespace, service.Name, err))\n   134→\t\t} else {\n   135→\t\t\tr.endpointSliceTracker.ExpectDeletion(sliceToDelete)\n   136→\t\t\tmetrics.EndpointSliceChanges.WithLabelValues(\"delete\").Inc()\n   137→\t\t}\n   138→\t}\n   139→\n   140→\treturn utilerrors.NewAggregate(errs)\n   141→}\n   142→\n   143→// reconcileByAddressType takes a set of pods currently matching a service selector and\n   144→// compares them with the endpoints already present in any existing endpoint\n   145→// slices (by address type) for the given service. It creates, updates, or deletes endpoint slices\n   146→// to ensure the desired set of pods are represented by endpoint slices.\n   147→func (r *Reconciler) reconcileByAddressType(logger klog.Logger, service *corev1.Service, pods []*corev1.Pod, existingSlices []*discovery.EndpointSlice, triggerTime time.Time, addressType discovery.AddressType) error {\n   148→\terrs := []error{}\n   149→\n   150→\tslicesToCreate := []*discovery.EndpointSlice{}\n   151→\tslicesToUpdate := []*discovery.EndpointSlice{}\n   152→\tslicesToDelete := []*discovery.EndpointSlice{}\n   153→\tevents := []*topologycache.EventBuilder{}\n   154→\n   155→\t// Build data structures for existing state.\n   156→\texistingSlicesByPortMap := map[endpointsliceutil.PortMapKey][]*discovery.EndpointSlice{}\n   157→\tfor _, existingSlice := range existingSlices {\n   158→\t\tif ownedBy(existingSlice, service) {\n   159→\t\t\tepHash := endpointsliceutil.NewPortMapKey(existingSlice.Ports)\n   160→\t\t\texistingSlicesByPortMap[epHash] = append(existingSlicesByPortMap[epHash], existingSlice)\n   161→\t\t} else {\n   162→\t\t\tslicesToDelete = append(slicesToDelete, existingSlice)\n   163→\t\t}\n   164→\t}\n   165→\n   166→\t// Build data structures for desired state.\n   167→\tdesiredMetaByPortMap := map[endpointsliceutil.PortMapKey]*endpointMeta{}\n   168→\tdesiredEndpointsByPortMap := map[endpointsliceutil.PortMapKey]endpointsliceutil.EndpointSet{}\n   169→\n   170→\tfor _, pod := range pods {\n   171→\t\tif !endpointsliceutil.ShouldPodBeInEndpoints(pod, true) {\n   172→\t\t\tcontinue\n   173→\t\t}\n   174→\n   175→\t\tendpointPorts := getEndpointPorts(logger, service, pod)\n   176→\t\tepHash := endpointsliceutil.NewPortMapKey(endpointPorts)\n   177→\t\tif _, ok := desiredEndpointsByPortMap[epHash]; !ok {\n   178→\t\t\tdesiredEndpointsByPortMap[epHash] = endpointsliceutil.EndpointSet{}\n   179→\t\t}\n   180→\n   181→\t\tif _, ok := desiredMetaByPortMap[epHash]; !ok {\n   182→\t\t\tdesiredMetaByPortMap[epHash] = &endpointMeta{\n   183→\t\t\t\taddressType: addressType,\n   184→\t\t\t\tports:       endpointPorts,\n   185→\t\t\t}\n   186→\t\t}\n   187→\n   188→\t\tnode, err := r.nodeLister.Get(pod.Spec.NodeName)\n   189→\t\tif err != nil {\n   190→\t\t\t// we are getting the information from the local informer,\n   191→\t\t\t// an error different than IsNotFound should not happen\n   192→\t\t\tif !errors.IsNotFound(err) {\n   193→\t\t\t\treturn err\n   194→\t\t\t}\n   195→\t\t\t// If the Node specified by the Pod doesn't exist we want to requeue the Service so we\n   196→\t\t\t// retry later, but also update the EndpointSlice without the problematic Pod.\n   197→\t\t\t// Theoretically, the pod Garbage Collector will remove the Pod, but we want to avoid\n   198→\t\t\t// situations where a reference from a Pod to a missing node can leave the EndpointSlice\n   199→\t\t\t// stuck forever.\n   200→\t\t\t// On the other side, if the service.Spec.PublishNotReadyAddresses is set we just add the\n   201→\t\t\t// Pod, since the user is explicitly indicating that the Pod address should be published.\n   202→\t\t\tif !service.Spec.PublishNotReadyAddresses {\n   203→\t\t\t\tlogger.Info(\"skipping Pod for Service, Node not found\", \"pod\", klog.KObj(pod), \"service\", klog.KObj(service), \"node\", klog.KRef(\"\", pod.Spec.NodeName))\n   204→\t\t\t\terrs = append(errs, fmt.Errorf(\"skipping Pod %s for Service %s/%s: Node %s Not Found\", pod.Name, service.Namespace, service.Name, pod.Spec.NodeName))\n   205→\t\t\t\tcontinue\n   206→\t\t\t}\n   207→\t\t}\n   208→\t\tendpoint := podToEndpoint(pod, node, service, addressType)\n   209→\t\tif len(endpoint.Addresses) > 0 {\n   210→\t\t\tdesiredEndpointsByPortMap[epHash].Insert(&endpoint)\n   211→\t\t}\n   212→\t}\n   213→\n   214→\tspMetrics := metrics.NewServicePortCache()\n   215→\ttotalAdded := 0\n   216→\ttotalRemoved := 0\n   217→\n   218→\t// Determine changes necessary for each group of slices by port map.\n   219→\tfor portMap, desiredEndpoints := range desiredEndpointsByPortMap {\n   220→\t\tnumEndpoints := len(desiredEndpoints)\n   221→\t\tpmSlicesToCreate, pmSlicesToUpdate, pmSlicesToDelete, added, removed := r.reconcileByPortMapping(\n   222→\t\t\tlogger, service, existingSlicesByPortMap[portMap], desiredEndpoints, desiredMetaByPortMap[portMap])\n   223→\n   224→\t\ttotalAdded += added\n   225→\t\ttotalRemoved += removed\n   226→\n   227→\t\tspMetrics.Set(portMap, metrics.EfficiencyInfo{\n   228→\t\t\tEndpoints: numEndpoints,\n   229→\t\t\tSlices:    len(existingSlicesByPortMap[portMap]) + len(pmSlicesToCreate) - len(pmSlicesToDelete),\n   230→\t\t})\n   231→\n   232→\t\tslicesToCreate = append(slicesToCreate, pmSlicesToCreate...)\n   233→\t\tslicesToUpdate = append(slicesToUpdate, pmSlicesToUpdate...)\n   234→\t\tslicesToDelete = append(slicesToDelete, pmSlicesToDelete...)\n   235→\t}\n   236→\n   237→\t// If there are unique sets of ports that are no longer desired, mark\n   238→\t// the corresponding endpoint slices for deletion.\n   239→\tfor portMap, existingSlices := range existingSlicesByPortMap {\n   240→\t\tif _, ok := desiredEndpointsByPortMap[portMap]; !ok {\n   241→\t\t\tslicesToDelete = append(slicesToDelete, existingSlices...)\n   242→\t\t}\n   243→\t}\n   244→\n   245→\t// When no endpoint slices would usually exist, we need to add a placeholder.\n   246→\tif len(existingSlices) == len(slicesToDelete) && len(slicesToCreate) < 1 {\n   247→\t\t// Check for existing placeholder slice outside of the core control flow\n   248→\t\tplaceholderSlice := newEndpointSlice(logger, service, &endpointMeta{ports: []discovery.EndpointPort{}, addressType: addressType}, r.controllerName)\n   249→\t\tif len(slicesToDelete) == 1 && placeholderSliceCompare.DeepEqual(slicesToDelete[0], placeholderSlice) {\n   250→\t\t\t// We are about to unnecessarily delete/recreate the placeholder, remove it now.\n   251→\t\t\tslicesToDelete = slicesToDelete[:0]\n   252→\t\t} else {\n   253→\t\t\tslicesToCreate = append(slicesToCreate, placeholderSlice)\n   254→\t\t}\n   255→\t\tspMetrics.Set(endpointsliceutil.NewPortMapKey(placeholderSlice.Ports), metrics.EfficiencyInfo{\n   256→\t\t\tEndpoints: 0,\n   257→\t\t\tSlices:    1,\n   258→\t\t})\n   259→\t}\n   260→\n   261→\tmetrics.EndpointsAddedPerSync.WithLabelValues().Observe(float64(totalAdded))\n   262→\tmetrics.EndpointsRemovedPerSync.WithLabelValues().Observe(float64(totalRemoved))\n   263→\n   264→\tserviceNN := types.NamespacedName{Name: service.Name, Namespace: service.Namespace}\n   265→\tr.metricsCache.UpdateServicePortCache(serviceNN, spMetrics)\n   266→\n   267→\t// Topology hints are assigned per address type. This means it is\n   268→\t// theoretically possible for endpoints of one address type to be assigned\n   269→\t// hints while another endpoints of another address type are not.\n   270→\tsi := &topologycache.SliceInfo{\n   271→\t\tServiceKey:  fmt.Sprintf(\"%s/%s\", service.Namespace, service.Name),\n   272→\t\tAddressType: addressType,\n   273→\t\tToCreate:    slicesToCreate,\n   274→\t\tToUpdate:    slicesToUpdate,\n   275→\t\tUnchanged:   unchangedSlices(existingSlices, slicesToUpdate, slicesToDelete),\n   276→\t}\n   277→\n   278→\tcanUseTrafficDistribution := r.trafficDistributionEnabled && !hintsEnabled(service.Annotations)\n   279→\n   280→\t// Check if we need to add/remove hints based on the topology annotation.\n   281→\t//\n   282→\t// This if/else clause can be removed once the annotation has been deprecated.\n   283→\t// Ref: https://github.com/kubernetes/enhancements/tree/master/keps/sig-network/4444-service-routing-preference\n   284→\tif r.topologyCache != nil && hintsEnabled(service.Annotations) {\n   285→\t\t// Reaching this point means that we need to configure hints based on the\n   286→\t\t// topology annotation.\n   287→\t\tslicesToCreate, slicesToUpdate, events = r.topologyCache.AddHints(logger, si)\n   288→\n   289→\t} else {\n   290→\t\t// Reaching this point means that we will not be configuring hints based on\n   291→\t\t// the topology annotation. We need to do 2 things:\n   292→\t\t//  1. If hints were added previously based on the annotation, we need to\n   293→\t\t//     clear up any locally cached hints from the topologyCache object.\n   294→\t\t//  2. Optionally remove the actual hints from the EndpointSlice if we know\n   295→\t\t//     that the `trafficDistribution` field is also NOT being used. In other\n   296→\t\t//     words, if we know that the `trafficDistribution` field has been\n   297→\t\t//     correctly configured by the customer, we DO NOT remove the hints and\n   298→\t\t//     wait for the trafficDist handlers to correctly configure them. Always\n   299→\t\t//     unconditionally removing hints here (and letting them get readded by\n   300→\t\t//     the trafficDist) adds extra overhead in the form of DeepCopy (done\n   301→\t\t//     within topologyCache.RemoveHints)\n   302→\n   303→\t\t// Check 1.\n   304→\t\tif r.topologyCache != nil {\n   305→\t\t\tif r.topologyCache.HasPopulatedHints(si.ServiceKey) {\n   306→\t\t\t\tlogger.Info(\"TopologyAwareHints annotation has changed, removing hints\", \"serviceKey\", si.ServiceKey, \"addressType\", si.AddressType)\n   307→\t\t\t\tevents = append(events, &topologycache.EventBuilder{\n   308→\t\t\t\t\tEventType: corev1.EventTypeWarning,\n   309→\t\t\t\t\tReason:    \"TopologyAwareHintsDisabled\",\n   310→\t\t\t\t\tMessage:   topologycache.FormatWithAddressType(topologycache.TopologyAwareHintsDisabled, si.AddressType),\n   311→\t\t\t\t})\n   312→\t\t\t}\n   313→\t\t\tr.topologyCache.RemoveHints(si.ServiceKey, addressType)\n   314→\t\t}\n   315→\n   316→\t\t// Check 2.\n   317→\t\tif !canUseTrafficDistribution {\n   318→\t\t\tslicesToCreate, slicesToUpdate = topologycache.RemoveHintsFromSlices(si)\n   319→\t\t}\n   320→\t}\n   321→\n   322→\tif canUseTrafficDistribution {\n   323→\t\tr.metricsCache.UpdateTrafficDistributionForService(serviceNN, service.Spec.TrafficDistribution)\n   324→\t\tslicesToCreate, slicesToUpdate, _ = trafficdist.ReconcileHints(service.Spec.TrafficDistribution, slicesToCreate, slicesToUpdate, unchangedSlices(existingSlices, slicesToUpdate, slicesToDelete))\n   325→\t} else {\n   326→\t\tr.metricsCache.UpdateTrafficDistributionForService(serviceNN, nil)\n   327→\t}\n   328→\n   329→\terr := r.finalize(service, slicesToCreate, slicesToUpdate, slicesToDelete, triggerTime)\n   330→\tif err != nil {\n   331→\t\terrs = append(errs, err)\n   332→\t}\n   333→\tfor _, event := range events {\n   334→\t\tr.eventRecorder.Event(service, event.EventType, event.Reason, event.Message)\n   335→\t}\n   336→\treturn utilerrors.NewAggregate(errs)\n   337→\n   338→}\n   339→\n   340→func NewReconciler(client clientset.Interface, nodeLister corelisters.NodeLister, maxEndpointsPerSlice int32, endpointSliceTracker *endpointsliceutil.EndpointSliceTracker, topologyCache *topologycache.TopologyCache, eventRecorder record.EventRecorder, controllerName string, options ...ReconcilerOption) *Reconciler {\n   341→\tr := &Reconciler{\n   342→\t\tclient:               client,\n   343→\t\tnodeLister:           nodeLister,\n   344→\t\tmaxEndpointsPerSlice: maxEndpointsPerSlice,\n   345→\t\tendpointSliceTracker: endpointSliceTracker,\n   346→\t\tmetricsCache:         metrics.NewCache(maxEndpointsPerSlice),\n   347→\t\ttopologyCache:        topologyCache,\n   348→\t\teventRecorder:        eventRecorder,\n   349→\t\tcontrollerName:       controllerName,\n   350→\t}\n   351→\tfor _, option := range options {\n   352→\t\toption(r)\n   353→\t}\n   354→\treturn r\n   355→}\n   356→\n   357→// placeholderSliceCompare is a conversion func for comparing two placeholder endpoint slices.\n   358→// It only compares the specific fields we care about.\n   359→var placeholderSliceCompare = conversion.EqualitiesOrDie(\n   360→\tfunc(a, b metav1.OwnerReference) bool {\n   361→\t\treturn a.String() == b.String()\n   362→\t},\n   363→\tfunc(a, b metav1.ObjectMeta) bool {\n   364→\t\tif a.Namespace != b.Namespace {\n   365→\t\t\treturn false\n   366→\t\t}\n   367→\t\tfor k, v := range a.Labels {\n   368→\t\t\tif b.Labels[k] != v {\n   369→\t\t\t\treturn false\n   370→\t\t\t}\n   371→\t\t}\n   372→\t\tfor k, v := range b.Labels {\n   373→\t\t\tif a.Labels[k] != v {\n   374→\t\t\t\treturn false\n   375→\t\t\t}\n   376→\t\t}\n   377→\t\treturn true\n   378→\t},\n   379→)\n   380→\n   381→// finalize creates, updates, and deletes slices as specified\n   382→func (r *Reconciler) finalize(\n   383→\tservice *corev1.Service,\n   384→\tslicesToCreate,\n   385→\tslicesToUpdate,\n   386→\tslicesToDelete []*discovery.EndpointSlice,\n   387→\ttriggerTime time.Time,\n   388→) error {\n   389→\t// If there are slices to create and delete, change the creates to updates\n   390→\t// of the slices that would otherwise be deleted.\n   391→\tfor i := 0; i < len(slicesToDelete); {\n   392→\t\tif len(slicesToCreate) == 0 {\n   393→\t\t\tbreak\n   394→\t\t}\n   395→\t\tsliceToDelete := slicesToDelete[i]\n   396→\t\tslice := slicesToCreate[len(slicesToCreate)-1]\n   397→\t\t// Only update EndpointSlices that are owned by this Service and have\n   398→\t\t// the same AddressType. We need to avoid updating EndpointSlices that\n   399→\t\t// are being garbage collected for an old Service with the same name.\n   400→\t\t// The AddressType field is immutable. Since Services also consider\n   401→\t\t// IPFamily immutable, the only case where this should matter will be\n   402→\t\t// the migration from IP to IPv4 and IPv6 AddressTypes, where there's a\n   403→\t\t// chance EndpointSlices with an IP AddressType would otherwise be\n   404→\t\t// updated to IPv4 or IPv6 without this check.\n   405→\t\tif sliceToDelete.AddressType == slice.AddressType && ownedBy(sliceToDelete, service) {\n   406→\t\t\tslice.Name = sliceToDelete.Name\n   407→\t\t\tslicesToCreate = slicesToCreate[:len(slicesToCreate)-1]\n   408→\t\t\tslicesToUpdate = append(slicesToUpdate, slice)\n   409→\t\t\tslicesToDelete = append(slicesToDelete[:i], slicesToDelete[i+1:]...)\n   410→\t\t} else {\n   411→\t\t\ti++\n   412→\t\t}\n   413→\t}\n   414→\n   415→\t// Don't create new EndpointSlices if the Service is pending deletion. This\n   416→\t// is to avoid a potential race condition with the garbage collector where\n   417→\t// it tries to delete EndpointSlices as this controller replaces them.\n   418→\tif service.DeletionTimestamp == nil {\n   419→\t\tfor _, endpointSlice := range slicesToCreate {\n   420→\t\t\taddTriggerTimeAnnotation(endpointSlice, triggerTime)\n   421→\t\t\tcreatedSlice, err := r.client.DiscoveryV1().EndpointSlices(service.Namespace).Create(context.TODO(), endpointSlice, metav1.CreateOptions{})\n   422→\t\t\tif err != nil {\n   423→\t\t\t\t// If the namespace is terminating, creates will continue to fail. Simply drop the item.\n   424→\t\t\t\tif errors.HasStatusCause(err, corev1.NamespaceTerminatingCause) {\n   425→\t\t\t\t\treturn nil\n   426→\t\t\t\t}\n   427→\t\t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"failed to create EndpointSlice for Service %s/%s: %v\", service.Namespace, service.Name, err)\n   428→\t\t\t}\n   429→\t\t\tr.endpointSliceTracker.Update(createdSlice)\n   430→\t\t\tmetrics.EndpointSliceChanges.WithLabelValues(\"create\").Inc()\n   431→\t\t}\n   432→\t}\n   433→\n   434→\tfor _, endpointSlice := range slicesToUpdate {\n   435→\t\taddTriggerTimeAnnotation(endpointSlice, triggerTime)\n   436→\t\tupdatedSlice, err := r.client.DiscoveryV1().EndpointSlices(service.Namespace).Update(context.TODO(), endpointSlice, metav1.UpdateOptions{})\n   437→\t\tif err != nil {\n   438→\t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"failed to update %s EndpointSlice for Service %s/%s: %v\", endpointSlice.Name, service.Namespace, service.Name, err)\n   439→\t\t}\n   440→\t\tr.endpointSliceTracker.Update(updatedSlice)\n   441→\t\tmetrics.EndpointSliceChanges.WithLabelValues(\"update\").Inc()\n   442→\t}\n   443→\n   444→\tfor _, endpointSlice := range slicesToDelete {\n   445→\t\terr := r.client.DiscoveryV1().EndpointSlices(service.Namespace).Delete(context.TODO(), endpointSlice.Name, metav1.DeleteOptions{})\n   446→\t\tif err != nil {\n   447→\t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"failed to delete %s EndpointSlice for Service %s/%s: %v\", endpointSlice.Name, service.Namespace, service.Name, err)\n   448→\t\t}\n   449→\t\tr.endpointSliceTracker.ExpectDeletion(endpointSlice)\n   450→\t\tmetrics.EndpointSliceChanges.WithLabelValues(\"delete\").Inc()\n   451→\t}\n   452→\n   453→\ttopologyLabel := \"Disabled\"\n   454→\tif r.topologyCache != nil && hintsEnabled(service.Annotations) {\n   455→\t\ttopologyLabel = \"Auto\"\n   456→\t}\n   457→\tvar trafficDistribution string\n   458→\tif r.trafficDistributionEnabled && !hintsEnabled(service.Annotations) {\n   459→\t\tif service.Spec.TrafficDistribution != nil && *service.Spec.TrafficDistribution == corev1.ServiceTrafficDistributionPreferClose {\n   460→\t\t\ttrafficDistribution = *service.Spec.TrafficDistribution\n   461→\t\t}\n   462→\t}\n   463→\n   464→\tnumSlicesChanged := len(slicesToCreate) + len(slicesToUpdate) + len(slicesToDelete)\n   465→\tmetrics.EndpointSlicesChangedPerSync.WithLabelValues(topologyLabel, trafficDistribution).Observe(float64(numSlicesChanged))\n   466→\n   467→\treturn nil\n   468→}\n   469→\n   470→// reconcileByPortMapping compares the endpoints found in existing slices with\n   471→// the list of desired endpoints and returns lists of slices to create, update,\n   472→// and delete. It also checks that the slices mirror the parent services labels.\n   473→// The logic is split up into several main steps:\n   474→//  1. Iterate through existing slices, delete endpoints that are no longer\n   475→//     desired and update matching endpoints that have changed. It also checks\n   476→//     if the slices have the labels of the parent services, and updates them if not.\n   477→//  2. Iterate through slices that have been modified in 1 and fill them up with\n   478→//     any remaining desired endpoints.\n   479→//  3. If there still desired endpoints left, try to fit them into a previously\n   480→//     unchanged slice and/or create new ones.\n   481→func (r *Reconciler) reconcileByPortMapping(\n   482→\tlogger klog.Logger,\n   483→\tservice *corev1.Service,\n   484→\texistingSlices []*discovery.EndpointSlice,\n   485→\tdesiredSet endpointsliceutil.EndpointSet,\n   486→\tendpointMeta *endpointMeta,\n   487→) ([]*discovery.EndpointSlice, []*discovery.EndpointSlice, []*discovery.EndpointSlice, int, int) {\n   488→\tslicesByName := map[string]*discovery.EndpointSlice{}\n   489→\tsliceNamesUnchanged := sets.New[string]()\n   490→\tsliceNamesToUpdate := sets.New[string]()\n   491→\tsliceNamesToDelete := sets.New[string]()\n   492→\tnumRemoved := 0\n   493→\n   494→\t// 1. If we still have desired endpoints to add and slices marked for update,\n   550→\t//    iterate through the slices and fill them up with the desired endpoints.\n   551→\tif desiredSet.Len() > 0 && sliceNamesToUpdate.Len() > 0 {\n   552→\t\tslices := []*discovery.EndpointSlice{}\n   553→\t\tfor _, sliceName := range sliceNamesToUpdate.UnsortedList() {\n   554→\t\t\tslices = append(slices, slicesByName[sliceName])\n   555→\t\t}\n   556→\t\t// Sort endpoint slices by length so we're filling up the fullest ones\n   557→\t\t// first.\n   558→\t\tsort.Sort(endpointSliceEndpointLen(slices))\n   559→\n   560→\t\t// Iterate through slices and fill them up with desired endpoints.\n   561→\t\tfor _, slice := range slices {\n   562→\t\t\tfor desiredSet.Len() > 0 && len(slice.Endpoints) < int(r.maxEndpointsPerSlice) {\n   563→\t\t\t\tendpoint, _ := desiredSet.PopAny()\n   564→\t\t\t\tslice.Endpoints = append(slice.Endpoints, *endpoint)\n   565→\t\t\t}\n   566→\t\t}\n   567→\t}\n   568→\n   569→\t// 3. If there are no slices with\n   571→\t//    that capacity, we create new slices for the endpoints.\n   572→\tslicesToCreate := []*discovery.EndpointSlice{}\n   573→\n   574→\tfor desiredSet.Len() > 0 haven't already been\n   579→\t\t// filled, try to fit them in one.\n   580→\t\tif desiredSet.Len() < int(r.maxEndpointsPerSlice) && sliceNamesUnchanged.Len() > 0 {\n   581→\t\t\tunchangedSlices := 584→\t\t\t}\n   585→\t\t\tsliceToFill = getSliceToFill(unchangedSlices, desiredSet.Len(), int(r.maxEndpointsPerSlice))\n   586→\t\t}\n   587→\n   588→\t\t// If we didn't find a sliceToFill, generate a new empty one.\n   589→\t\tif sliceToFill == nil {\n   590→\t\t\tsliceToFill = newEndpointSlice(logger, service, endpointMeta, r.controllerName)\n   591→\t\t} else {\n   592→\t\t\t// deep copy required to modify this slice.\n   593→\t\t\tsliceToFill = sliceToFill.DeepCopy()\n   594→\t\t\tslicesByName[sliceToFill.Name] = sliceToFill\n   595→\t\t}\n   596→\n   597→\t\t// Fill the slice up with remaining endpoints.\n   598→\t\tfor desiredSet.Len() > 0 && len(sliceToFill.Endpoints) < int(r.maxEndpointsPerSlice) {\n   599→\t\t\tendpoint, _ := desiredSet.PopAny()\n   600→\t\t\tsliceToFill.Endpoints = append(sliceToFill.Endpoints, *endpoint)\n   601→\t\t}\n   602→\n   603→\t\t// New slices will not have a Name set, use this to determine whether\n   604→\t\t// this should be an update or create.\n   605→\t\tif sliceToFill.Name != \"\" {\n   606→\t\t\tsliceNamesToUpdate.Insert(sliceToFill.Name)\n   607→\t\t\tsliceNamesUnchanged.Delete(sliceToFill.Name)\n   608→\t\t} else {\n   609→\t\t\tslicesToCreate = append(slicesToCreate, sliceToFill)\n   610→\t\t}\n   611→\t}\n   612→\n   613→\t// Build slicesToUpdate from slice names.\n   614→\tslicesToUpdate := []*discovery.EndpointSlice{}\n   615→\tfor _, sliceName := range sliceNamesToUpdate.UnsortedList() {\n   616→\t\tslicesToUpdate = append(slicesToUpdate, slicesByName[sliceName])\n   617→\t}\n   618→\n   619→\t// Build slicesToDelete from slice names.\n   620→\tslicesToDelete := []*discovery.EndpointSlice{}\n   621→\tfor _, sliceName := range sliceNamesToDelete.UnsortedList() {\n   622→\t\tslicesToDelete = append(slicesToDelete, slicesByName[sliceName])\n   623→\t}\n   624→\n   625→\treturn slicesToCreate, slicesToUpdate, slicesToDelete, numAdded, numRemoved\n   626→}\n   627→\n   628→func (r *Reconciler) DeleteService(namespace, name string) {\n   629→\tr.metricsCache.DeleteService(types.NamespacedName{Namespace: namespace, Name: name})\n   630→}\n   631→\n   632→func (r This\n   135→\t// handler will lookup the owner of the given Deployment, and if it is\n   136→\t// owned by a Foo resource then the handler will enqueue that Foo resource for\n   137→\t// processing. It will block until stopCh\n   160→// is closed, at which point it will shutdown the workqueue and wait for\n   161→// workers to finish processing their current work items.\n   162→func (c *Controller) Run(ctx context.Context, workers int) error {\n   163→\tdefer utilruntime.HandleCrash()\n   164→\tdefer c.workqueue.ShutDown()\n   165→\tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n   166→\n   167→\t// Start the informer factories to begin populating the informer caches\n   168→\tlogger.Info(\"Starting Foo controller\")\n   169→\n   170→\t// Wait for the caches to be synced before starting workers\n   171→\tlogger.Info(\"Waiting for informer caches to sync\")\n   172→\n   173→\tif ok := cache.WaitForCacheSync(ctx.Done(), c.deploymentsSynced, c.foosSynced); !ok {\n   174→\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"failed to wait for caches to sync\")\n   175→\t}\n   176→\n   177→\tlogger.Info(\"Starting workers\", \"count\", workers)\n   178→\t// Launch two workers to process Foo resources\n   179→\tfor i := 0; We also must remember to call Forget\n   210→\t// if we do not want this work item being re-queued. For example, we do\n   211→\t// not call Forget if a transient error occurs, instead the item is\n   212→\t// put back on the workqueue and attempted again after a back-off\n   213→\t// period.\n   214→\tdefer c.workqueue.Done(objRef)\n   215→\n   216→\t// Run the syncHandler, passing it the structured reference to the object to be synced.\n   217→\terr := c.syncHandler(ctx, objRef)\n   218→\tif err == nil {\n   219→\t\t// If no error occurs then we Forget this item so it does not\n   220→\t\t// get queued again until another change happens.\n   221→\t\tc.workqueue.Forget(objRef)\n   222→\t\tlogger.Info(\"Successfully synced\", \"objectName\", objRef)\n   223→\t\treturn true\n   224→\t}\n   225→\t// there was a failure so be sure to report it.  This method allows for\n   226→\t// pluggable error handling which can be used for things like\n   227→\t// cluster-monitoring.\n   228→\tutilruntime.HandleErrorWithContext(ctx, err, \"Error syncing; requeuing for later retry\", \"objectReference\", objRef)\n   229→\t// since we failed, we should requeue the item to work on later.  This\n   230→\t// method will add a backoff to avoid hotlooping on particular items\n   231→\t// (they're probably still not going to work right away) and overall\n   232→\t// controller protection (everything I've done is broken, this controller\n   233→\t// needs to calm down or it can starve other useful work) cases.\n   234→\tc.workqueue.AddRateLimited(objRef)\n   235→\treturn true\n   236→}\n   237→\n   238→// syncHandler compares the actual state with the desired, and attempts to\n   239→// converge the two. 96→}\n    97→\n    98→// PeerEndpointController is the controller manager for updating the peer endpoint leases.\n    99→// This provides a separate independent reconciliation loop for peer endpoint leases\n   100→// which ensures that the peer kube-apiservers are fetching the updated endpoint info for a given apiserver\n   101→// in the case when the peer wants to proxy the request to the given apiserver because it can not serve the\n   102→// request itself due to version mismatch.\n   103→type PeerEndpointLeaseController struct {\n   104→\treconciler       PeerEndpointLeaseReconciler\n   105→\tendpointInterval time.Duration\n   106→\tserverId         string\n   107→\t// peeraddress stores the IP and port of this kube-apiserver. Used by peer kube-apiservers to\n   108→\t// route request to this apiserver in case of a version skew.\n   109→\tpeeraddress string\n   110→\n   111→\tclient kubernetes.Interface\n   112→\n   113→\tlock   sync.Mutex\n   114→\tstopCh chan struct{} // closed by Stop()\n   115→}\n   116→\n   117→func New(serverId string, peeraddress string,\n   118→\treconciler PeerEndpointLeaseReconciler, endpointInterval time.Duration, client kubernetes.Interface) *PeerEndpointLeaseController {\n   119→\treturn &PeerEndpointLeaseController{\n   120→\t\treconciler: reconciler,\n   121→\t\tserverId:   serverId,\n   122→\t\t// peeraddress stores the IP and port of this kube-apiserver. This makes sure that at least some of\n   214→\t// the servers will add our endpoint lease.\n   215→\tif err := c.reconciler.UpdateLease(c.serverId, host, endpointPorts); err != nil {\n   216→\t\treturn err\n   217→\t}\n   218→\treturn nil\n   219→}\n   220→\n   221→// UpdateLease resets the TTL on a server IP in storage\n   222→// UpdateLease will create a new key if it doesn't exist.\n   223→// We use the first element in endpointPorts as a part of the lease's base key\n   224→// This is done to support out tests that simulate 2 apiservers running on the same ip but\n   225→// different ports\n   226→\n   227→// It will also do the following if UnknownVersionInteroperabilityProxy feature is enabled\n   228→// 1. store the apiserverId as a label\n   229→// 2. store the values passed to --peer-advertise-ip and --peer-advertise-port flags to kube-apiserver as an annotation\n   230→// with value of format <ip:port>\n   231→func (r *peerEndpointLeaseReconciler) UpdateLease(serverId string, ip string, endpointPorts []corev1.EndpointPort) error {\n   232→\t// reconcile endpoints only if apiserver was not shutdown\n   233→\tif r.stopReconcilingCalled.Load() {\n   234→\t\treturn nil\n   235→\t}\n   236→\n   237→\t// we use the serverID as the key to avoid using the server IP, port as the key.\n   238→\t// note: this means that this lease doesn't enforce Instead, it uses a custom controller management pattern based on work queues and informers. Here is how controllers register and reconcile in kubernetes/kubernetes:\\n\\n## Controller Registration Pattern\\n\\nControllers are registered through the ControllerDescriptor system defined in cmd/kube-controller-manager/app/controllermanager.go:\\n\\n1. **NewControllerDescriptors()** (line 495) - Registers all known controllers. Each controller descriptor contains:\\n   - A unique name (e.g., 'endpointslice-controller')\\n   - An initFunc that initializes the controller\\n   - Optional aliases\\n   - Feature gate requirements\\n\\n2. **ControllerDescriptor** - Contains:\\n   - name: string\\n   - aliases: []string  \\n   - initFunc: function that creates and starts the controller\\n   - requiresSpecialHandling: bool (for controllers like ServiceAccountTokenController that must start first)\\n\\n3. **ControllerContext** (line 366) - Passed to each controller's initFunc containing:\\n   - ClientBuilder: for creating API clients\\n   - InformerFactory: SharedInformerFactory for watching resources\\n   - ObjectOrMetadataInformerFactory: for metadata access\\n   - RESTMapper: for resource mapping\\n   - ResyncPeriod: function generating sync intervals\\n\\n## Controller Startup Flow\\n\\n1. **StartControllers()** (line 662) - Main function that starts all registered controllers\\n2. **StartController()** (line 710) - Starts an individual controller by:\\n   - Checking feature gate requirements\\n   - Calling the controller's initFunc\\n   - Starting worker goroutines\\n\\n## Reconciliation Pattern (Non-Controller-Runtime)\\n\\nInstead of the controller-runtime Reconciler interface, Kubernetes uses:\\n\\n### Work Queue Pattern (Standard)\\nSeen in staging/src/k8s.io/sample-controller/controller.go:\\n- Controller struct with:\\n  - workqueue.RateLimitingInterface for queuing work items\\n  - Informer synced callbacks for coordinating startup\\n  - Event recorder for recording cluster events\\n\\n- Run(ctx, workers) - Main loop that:\\n  - Waits for informer caches to sync (WaitForCacheSync)\\n  - Launches N worker goroutines\\n  - Each worker calls runWorker -> processNextWorkItem -> syncHandler\\n\\n- syncHandler(ctx, objectRef) - The reconciliation logic that:\\n  - Gets the object from lister\\n  - Compares desired vs actual state\\n  - Performs operations to converge state\\n  - Handles errors with backoff/requeuing\\n\\n### Endpoint Reconciler Pattern (Custom)\\nSeen in pkg/controlplane/reconcilers/reconcilers.go:\\n- EndpointReconciler interface with methods:\\n  - ReconcileEndpoints() - Reconciles master endpoints\\n  - RemoveEndpoints() - Removes endpoint entries\\n  - StopReconciling() - Cleanly stops reconciliation\\n  - Destroy() - Cleans up resources\\n\\n- Implementations:\\n  - masterCountEndpointReconciler (instancecount.go) - Reconciles based on expected master count\\n  - leaseEndpointReconciler (lease.go) - Stores endpoint info using leases\\n\\n### Apiserver Reconciler Pattern\\nSeen in staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/reconcilers/peer_endpoint_lease.go:\\n- PeerEndpointLeaseReconciler interface for managing apiserver peer endpoints\\n- PeerEndpointLeaseController struct with:\\n  - Run(stopCh) - Main reconciliation loop\\n  - UpdatePeerEndpointLeases() - Periodic reconciliation function\\n  - Fixed interval polling (not event-driven)\\n\\n## Key Differences from Controller-Runtime\\n\\n1. **No Manager**: Controllers are started directly, not registered with a manager\\n2. **No Reconcile Interface**: Controllers implement custom Run/sync methods, not Reconcile(ctx, Request) (Result, error)\\n3. **Work Queue Based**: Uses client-go's workqueue.RateLimitingInterface, not controller-runtime's reconcile.Request/Result\\n4. **Manual Startup**: Controllers initialize event handlers and workers directly via cache.ResourceEventHandlerFuncs\\n5. **No SetupWithManager**: Controllers don't have a SetupWithManager method -
